# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes API Server Admission Controller Chain

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the API server admission controller pipeline: the admission.Interface registration, the generic admission chain execution, the mutating admission ordering, and the validating admission webhook call.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've successfully created a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes API server admission controller pipeline. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've identified **17 Go source files** in `kubernetes/kubernetes` that implement the complete API server admission controller pipeline:

### Core Components:

1. **Interface Definitions** (`interfaces.go`): `Interface`, `MutationInterface`, `ValidationInterface`
2. **Chain Execution** (`chain.go`): `chainAdmissionHandler` that sequentially executes admission checks
3. **Plugin Registry** (`plugins.go`): `Plugins` struct and `NewFromPlugins` to assemble the admission chain
4. **Reinvocation** (`reinvocation.go`): `reinvoker` wrapper handling webhook reinvocation policies
5. **Configuration** (`server/options/admission.go`): `AdmissionOptions` and `ApplyTo` for setup
6. **Mutating Webhook**: Plugin and dispatcher for mutations
7. **Validating Webhook**: Plugin and dispatcher for validations
8. **Metrics & Decorators**: Wrapping plugins with metrics and other decorators
9. **Kubernetes-specific Config**: Plugin ordering and defaults

### Execution Flow:

The pipeline follows this sequence:
1. Plugin Registration (via `RegisterAllAdmissionPlugins`)
2. Configuration Setup (via `AdmissionOptions.ApplyTo`)
3. Chain Construction (via `NewFromPlugins`)
4. Request Flow: Mutation Phase → Validation Phase → Webhook Dispatch → Optional Reinvocation

The complete analysis has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed documentation of all files, symbols, the execution chain, and a comprehensive narrative explanation of the architecture.

For MutationInterface handlers, calls Admit and returns on first error.\\n- `Validate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error`: Similarly iterates and calls Validate on ValidationInterface handlers.\\n- `Handles(operation Operation) bool`: Returns true if any handler handles the operation.\\n\\n### Plugin Registration and Initialization\\n\\n**File: staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugins.go**\\n\\nThe `Plugins` struct manages plugin registration and instantiation:\\n- `Register(name string, plugin Factory)`: Registers admission plugin factories with unique names.\\n- `NewFromPlugins(pluginNames []string, configProvider ConfigProvider, pluginInitializer PluginInitializer, decorator Decorator)`: Creates an admission chain from plugin names:\\n  1. Determines enabled plugins from flags and defaults\\n  2. Creates generic and custom plugin initializers\\n  3. Calls `NewFromPlugins` to build the complete admission chain\\n  4. Wraps the chain with metrics via `WithStepMetrics`\\n  5. Sets as `c.AdmissionControl` on the server config\\n\\n### Mutating Admission Webhook\\n\\n**File: staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/plugin.go**\\n\\nThe `Plugin` struct implements `MutationInterface`:\\n- `NewMutatingWebhook(configFile io.Reader)`: Creates a mutating webhook plugin with a dispatcher for calling external webhooks.\\n- `Admit(ctx context.Context, attr admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces)`: Delegates to `Webhook.Dispatch` to invoke the webhook handlers.\\n\\n**File: staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go**\\n\\nThe `mutatingDispatcher` handles webhook dispatch for mutations:\\n- `Dispatch(ctx context.Context, attr admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces, hooks []webhook.WebhookAccessor)`: Iterates through webhook configurations and:\\n  1. Checks webhook rules match the request\\n  2. Constructs VersionedAttributes for each webhook\\n  3. Calls webhook endpoints with AdmissionReview\\n  4. Applies JSON patches from webhook responses\\n  5. Manages reinvocation context for webhook reinvocations\\n\\n### Validating Admission Webhook\\n\\n**File: staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/plugin.go**\\n\\nThe `Plugin` struct implements `ValidationInterface`:\\n- `NewValidatingAdmissionWebhook(configFile io.Reader)`: Creates a validating webhook plugin.\\n- `Validate(ctx context.Context, attr admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces)`: Delegates to `Webhook.Dispatch` for validation.\\n\\n**File: staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/dispatcher.go**\\n\\nThe `validatingDispatcher` handles webhook dispatch for validations:\\n- `Dispatch(ctx context.Context, attr admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces, hooks []webhook.WebhookAccessor)`: Similar to mutating dispatcher but:\\n  1. Does NOT apply patches (only validates)\\n  2. Returns errors if validation fails\\n  3. Server startup: `NewAdmissionOptions()` creates options with plugin registry\\n2. Configuration: `ApplyTo()` reads enabled plugins and config files\\n3. Chain construction: `NewFromPlugins()` instantiates plugins and creates chainAdmissionHandler\\n4. Request handling: Admission.Admit() calls chainAdmissionHandler.Admit()\\n5. Validation phase: chainAdmissionHandler iterates handlers, calling Validate() on ValidationInterface plugins\\n7. For MutationInterface handlers, calls Admit and returns on first error.\\n- `Validate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error`: Similarly iterates and calls Validate on ValidationInterface handlers.\\n- `Handles(operation Operation) bool`: Returns true if any handler handles the operation.\\n\\n### Plugin Registration and Initialization\\n\\n**File: staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugins.go**\\n\\nThe `Plugins` struct manages plugin registration and instantiation:\\n- `Register(name string, plugin Factory)`: Registers admission plugin factories with unique names.\\n- `NewFromPlugins(pluginNames []string, configProvider ConfigProvider, pluginInitializer PluginInitializer, decorator Decorator)`: Creates an admission chain from plugin names:\\n  1.
